ns-0 ns-subject page-Highland_games rootpage-Highland_games skin-vector action-view">\t\t<div id="mw-page-base" class="noprint"></div>\n\t\t<div id="mw-head-base" class="noprint"></div>\n\t\t<div id="content" class="mw-body" role="main">\n\t\t\t<a id="top"></a>\n\t\t\t<div id="siteNotice" class="mw-body-content"><!-- CentralNotice --></div><div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n</div>\n<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Highland games</h1>\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"></div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Highland_Games-Opening_ceremonies_in_Canmore.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Highland_Games-Opening_ceremonies_in_Canmore.jpg/220px-Highland_Games-Opening_ceremonies_in_Canmore.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Highland_Games-Opening_ceremonies_in_Canmore.jpg/330px-Highland_Games-Opening_ceremonies_in_Canmore.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Highland_Games-Opening_ceremonies_in_Canmore.jpg/440px-Highland_Games-Opening_ceremonies_in_Canmore.jpg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Highland_Games-Opening_ceremonies_in_Canmore.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Opening ceremonies of 2004 <a href="/wiki/Canmore,_Alberta" title="Canmore, Alberta">Canmore</a> Highland games</div></div></div>\n<p><b>Highland games</b> are events held in spring and summer in <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> and other countries as a way of celebrating Scottish and <a href="/wiki/Celt" class="mw-redirect" title="Celt">Celtic</a> culture, especially that of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Highlands" title="Scottish Highlands">Scottish Highlands</a>. Certain aspects of the games are so well known as to have become emblematic of Scotland, such as the <a href="/wiki/Bagpipes" title="Bagpipes">bagpipes</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kilt" title="Kilt">kilt</a>, and the heavy events, especially the <a href="/wiki/Caber_toss" title="Caber toss">caber toss</a>. While centred on competitions in piping and drumming, dancing, and Scottish heavy athletics, the games also include entertainment and exhibits related to other aspects of Scottish and <a href="/wiki/Gaels" title="Gaels">Gaelic</a> culture.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Cowal_Highland_Gathering" title="Cowal Highland Gathering">Cowal Highland Gathering</a>, better known as the <i>Cowal Games</i>, held in <a href="/wiki/Dunoon" title="Dunoon">Dunoon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, every August, is the largest Highland games in the world,<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Cowal"><a class="external autonumber" href="//en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Highland_games#endnote_Cowal">[1]</a></sup> attracting around 3,500 competitors and somewhere in the region of 23,000 spectators<sup id="cite_ref-CHG1_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CHG1-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> from around the globe. Worldwide, however, it is exceeded in terms of spectators by two gatherings in the United States: the estimated 30,000<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> that attend <a href="/wiki/Grandfather_Mountain" title="Grandfather Mountain">Grandfather Mountain</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a> and the even larger gathering\xe2\x80\x94the largest in the Northern Hemisphere<sup id="cite_ref-Scottish_Games_Draw_Record_Crowds_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scottish_Games_Draw_Record_Crowds-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\xe2\x80\x94that has taken place every year since 1866.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> This event is currently held on Labor Day weekend in <a href="/wiki/Pleasanton,_California" title="Pleasanton, California">Pleasanton, California</a>, and their Sesquicentennial Games held on September 5\xe2\x80\x936, 2015, attracted record crowds close to 50,000.<sup id="cite_ref-Scottish_Games_Draw_Record_Crowds_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scottish_Games_Draw_Record_Crowds-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The games are claimed to have influenced <a href="/wiki/Baron_Pierre_de_Coubertin" class="mw-redirect" title="Baron Pierre de Coubertin">Baron Pierre de Coubertin</a> when he was planning the <a href="/wiki/1896_Summer_Olympics#Reviving_the_Games" title="1896 Summer Olympics">revival of the Olympic Games</a>. De Coubertin saw a display of Highland games at the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Exhibition_of_1889" class="mw-redirect" title="Paris Exhibition of 1889">Paris Exhibition of 1889</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11"><a href="#Bermuda"><span class="tocnumber">4.3</span> <span class="toctext">Bermuda</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12"><a href="#Brazil"><span class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a href="#Hungary"><span class="tocnumber">4.7</span> <span class="toctext">Hungary</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a href="#Indonesia"><span href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Highland_games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The origin of human games and sports predates recorded history. An example of a possible early games venue is at <a href="/wiki/Fetteresso_Castle" title="Fetteresso Castle">Fetteresso</a>, although that location is technically a few miles south of the Scotland Highlands.\n</p><p>It is reported in numerous Highland games programs, that King <a href="/wiki/Malcolm_III_of_Scotland" title="Malcolm III of Scotland">Malcolm III of Scotland</a>, in the 11th century, summoned contestants to a foot race to the summit of Craig Choinnich (overlooking <a href="/wiki/Braemar" title="Braemar">Braemar</a>).<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Canmore"><a class="external autonumber" href="//en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Highland_games#endnote_Canmore">[2]</a></sup> King Malcolm created this foot race in order to find the fastest runner in the land to be his royal messenger. Some have seen this apocryphal event to be the origin of today\'s modern Highland games.<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_origins"><a class="external autonumber" href="//en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Highland_games#endnote_origins">[3]</a></sup>\n</p><p>There is a document from 1703 summoning the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_clan" title="Scottish clan">clan</a> of the Laird of Grant, <a href="/wiki/Clan_Grant" title="Clan Grant">Clan Grant</a>. They were to arrive wearing Highland coats and "also with <a href="/wiki/Long_gun" title="Long gun">gun</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sword" title="Sword">sword</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pistol" title="Pistol">pistol</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dirk" title="Dirk">dirk</a>".<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_Grant"><a class="external autonumber" href="//en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Highland_games#endnote_Grant">[4]</a></sup> From this letter, it is believed that the competitions would have included feats of arms.\n</p><p>However, the modern Highland games are largely a Victorian invention, developed after the Highland Clearances.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Events">Events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Highland_games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Heavy_events">Heavy events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Highland_games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Heavy events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Caber_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Caber_2.jpg/220px-Caber_2.jpg" width="220" height="431" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Caber_2.jpg/330px-Caber_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Caber_2.jpg/440px-Caber_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="499" data-file-height="978" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Caber_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A caber being thrown at the 2000 <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">New Hampshire</a> Highland Games</div></div></div><p> In their original form many centuries ago, Highland games revolved around athletic and sports competitions. Though other activities were always a part of the festivities, many today still consider Highland athletics to be what the games are all about\xe2\x80\x94in short, that the athletics are the Games, and all the other activities are just entertainment. Regardless, it remains true today that the athletic competitions are at least an integral part of the events and one\xe2\x80\x94the caber toss\xe2\x80\x94has come to almost symbolize the Highland games.\n</p><p>Although quite a range of events can be a part of the Highland athletics competition, a few have become standard.\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Caber_toss" title="Caber toss">Caber toss</a>: A long log is stood upright and hoisted by the competitor who balances it vertically holding the smaller end in his hands (see photo). Then the competitor runs forward attempting to toss it in such a way that it turns end over end with the upper (larger) end striking the ground first. The smaller end that was originally held by the athlete then hits the ground in the 12 o\'clock position measured relative to the direction of the run. If successful, the athlete is said to have turned the caber. Cabers vary greatly in length, weight, taper, and balance, all of which affect the <a href="/wiki/Degree_of_difficulty" title="Degree of difficulty">degree of difficulty</a> in making a successful toss. Competitors are judged on how closely their throws approximate the ideal 12 o\'clock toss on an imaginary clock.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Stone_put" title="Stone put">Stone put</a>: This event is similar to the modern-day <a href="/wiki/Shot_put" title="Shot put">shot put</a> as seen in the Olympic Games. Instead of a steel shot, a large stone of variable weight is often used. There are also some differences from the Olympic shot put in allowable techniques. There are two versions of the stone toss events, differing in allowable technique. The "Braemar Stone" uses a 20\xe2\x80\x9326&#160;lb stone for men (13\xe2\x80\x9318&#160;lb for women) and does not allow any run up to the toeboard or "trig" to deliver the stone, i.e., it is a standing put. In the "Open Stone" using a 16\xe2\x80\x9322&#160;lb stone for men (or 8\xe2\x80\x9312&#160;lb for women), the thrower is allowed to use any throwing style so long as the stone is put with one hand with the stone resting cradled in the neck until the moment of release. Most athletes in the open stone event use either the "glide" or the "spin" techniques.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Scottish_hammer_throw" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish hammer throw">Scottish hammer throw</a>: This event is similar to the <a href="/wiki/Hammer_throw" title="Hammer throw">hammer throw</a> as seen in modern-day track and field competitions, though with some differences. In the Scottish event, a round metal ball (weighing 16 or 22&#160;lb for men or 12 or 16&#160;lb for women) is attached to the end of a shaft about 4 feet in length and made out of wood, bamboo, rattan, or plastic. With the feet in a fixed position, the hammer is whirled about one\'s head and thrown for distance over the shoulder. Hammer throwers sometimes employ specially designed footwear with flat blades to dig into the turf to maintain their balance and resist the centrifugal forces of the implement as it is whirled about the head. This substantially increases the distance attainable in the throw.</li></ul>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Weight_throw,_2002_Celtic_Festival.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Weight_throw%2C_2002_Celtic_Festival.jpg/220px-Weight_throw%2C_2002_Celtic_Festival.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Weight_throw%2C_2002_Celtic_Festival.jpg/330px-Weight_throw%2C_2002_Celtic_Festival.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Weight_throw%2C_2002_Celtic_Festival.jpg/440px-Weight_throw%2C_2002_Celtic_Festival.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="767" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Weight_throw,_2002_Celtic_Festival.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Weight throw</div></div></div>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Weight_throw" title="Weight throw">Weight throw</a>, also known as the weight for distance event. There are actually two separate events, one using a light (28&#160;lb for men and 14&#160;lb for women) and the other a heavy (56&#160;lb for men, 42&#160;lb for masters men, and 28&#160;lb for women) weight. The weights are made of metal and have a handle attached either directly or by means of a chain. The implement is thrown using one hand only, but otherwise using any technique. Usually a spinning technique is employed. The longest throw wins.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Weight_over_the_bar" class="mw-redirect" title="Weight over the bar">Weight over the bar</a>, also known as weight for height. The athletes attempt to toss a 56-pound (4-<a href="/wiki/Stone_(unit)" title="Stone (unit)">stone</a>) weight with an attached handle over a horizontal bar using only one hand. Each athlete is allowed three attempts at each height. Successful clearance of the height allows the athlete to advance into the next round at a greater height. The competition is determined by the highest successful toss with fewest misses being used to break tie scores.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sheaf_toss" title="Sheaf toss">Sheaf toss</a>: A bundle of straw (the sheaf) weighing 20 pounds (9.1&#160;kg) for the men and 10 pounds (4.5&#160;kg) for the women and wrapped in a burlap bag is tossed vertically with a pitchfork over a raised bar much like that used in pole vaulting. The progression and scoring of this event is similar to the Weight Over The Bar. There is significant debate among athletes as to whether the sheaf toss is in fact an authentic Highland event. Some argue it is actually a country fair event, but all agree that it is a great crowd pleaser.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>\n<li><b>Maide-leisg</b> (Scots Gaelic meaning \'Lazy Stick\', <small>Scottish Gaelic pronunciation:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Help:IPA/Scottish Gaelic">[mat\xca\xb2\xc9\x99\'\xca\x8ee\xca\x83k\xca\xb2]</a></span>): Trial of strength performed by two men sitting on the ground with the soles of their feet pressing against each other. Thus seated, they held a stick between their hands which they pulled against each other until one of them was raised from the ground. The oldest \'Maide Leisg\' competition in the world takes place at the Carloway show and Highland Games on the Isle of Lewis.</li></ul>\n<p>Many of the Heavy Events competitors in Scottish highland athletics are former high school and college track and field athletes who find the Scottish games are a good way to continue their competitive careers.\n</p><p>Increasingly in the USA, the Heavy Events are attracting women and master class athletes which has led to a proliferation of additional classes in Heavy Events competitions. Lighter implements are used in the classes.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Highland_games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Massed_Bands,_2005_Pacific_Northwest_Highland_Games.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Massed_Bands%2C_2005_Pacific_Northwest_Highland_Games.jpg/220px-Massed_Bands%2C_2005_Pacific_Northwest_Highland_Games.jpg" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Massed_Bands%2C_2005_Pacific_Northwest_Highland_Games.jpg/330px-Massed_Bands%2C_2005_Pacific_Northwest_Highland_Games.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/63/Massed_Bands%2C_2005_Pacific_Northwest_Highland_Games.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="245" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Massed_Bands,_2005_Pacific_Northwest_Highland_Games.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Massed bands at the 2005 <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.sshga.org">Pacific Northwest Highland Games</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pipeband_circle.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Pipeband_circle.JPG/220px-Pipeband_circle.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Pipeband_circle.JPG/330px-Pipeband_circle.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Pipeband_circle.JPG/440px-Pipeband_circle.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pipeband_circle.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Highland Pipeband Competition Circle [Prince Charles Pipe Band 2008]</div></div></div>\n<p>For many Highland games festival attendees, the most memorable of all the events at the games is the massing of the pipe bands. Normally held in conjunction with the opening and closing ceremonies of the games, as many as 20 or more pipe bands will march and play together. The result is a thunderous rendition of <i><a href="/wiki/Scotland_the_Brave" title="Scotland the Brave">Scotland the Brave</a></i> or <i><a href="/wiki/Amazing_Grace" title="Amazing Grace">Amazing Grace</a></i>, and other crowd-pleasing favourites.\n</p><p>It is, in fact, the music of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Highland_Bagpipe" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Highland Bagpipe">bagpipe</a> which has come to symbolize music at the Games and, indeed, in <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> itself. In addition to the massed bands, nearly all Highland games gatherings feature a wide range of piping and drumming competition, including solo piping and drumming, small group ensembles and, of course, the pipe bands themselves.\n</p><p>Music at Highland games gatherings also includes other forms, such as <a href="/wiki/Fiddle" title="Fiddle">fiddling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harp" title="Harp">harp</a> circles and <a href="/wiki/Celt" class="mw-redirect" title="Celt">Celtic</a> bands, usually spiced with a large amount of bagpipe music.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dance">Dance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Highland_games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Dance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cowal_Highland_Gathering" title="Cowal Highland Gathering">Cowal Highland Gathering</a> hosts the annual World Highland Dancing Championship. This event gathers the best competitive dancers from around the world who compete for the <a href="/wiki/Highland_dancing#Organization" class="mw-redirect" title="Highland dancing">SOBHD</a> sanctioned World Championship title.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Secondary_events_and_attractions">Secondary events and attractions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Highland_games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Secondary events and attractions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2005_Tacoma_Highland_Games.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/2005_Tacoma_Highland_Games.jpg/220px-2005_Tacoma_Highland_Games.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/2005_Tacoma_Highland_Games.jpg/330px-2005_Tacoma_Highland_Games.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/45/2005_Tacoma_Highland_Games.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="300" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2005_Tacoma_Highland_Games.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Assembling for the parade of clans at the 2005 <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.tacomagames.org">Tacoma Highland Games</a></div></div></div>\n<p>At modern-day Highland Games events, a wide variety of other activities and events are generally available. Foremost among these are the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Clan" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Clan">clan</a> tents and vendors of Scottish related goods. The various clan societies make the Highland games one of the main focus of their seasonal activities, usually making an appearance at as many such events as possible. Visitors can find out information about the Scottish roots and can become active in their own clan society if they wish.\n</p><p>At modern games, armouries will display their collections of swords and armour, and often perform mock battles. Various vendors selling Scottish memorabilia are also present selling everything from <a href="/wiki/Irn-Bru" title="Irn-Bru">Irn-Bru</a> to the stuffed likeness of the <a href="/wiki/Loch_Ness_Monster" title="Loch Ness Monster">Loch Ness Monster</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Herding_dog" title="Herding dog">Herding dog</a> trials and exhibitions are often held, showcasing the breeder\'s and trainer\'s skills. In addition, there may be other types of Highland animals present, such as the <a href="/wiki/Highland_cattle" title="Highland cattle">Highland cattle</a>.\n</p><p>Various traditional and modern <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celtic</a> arts are often showcased. These could include harpers\' circles, <a href="/wiki/Scottish_country_dancing" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish country dancing">Scottish country dancing</a>, and one or more entertainment stages. In addition, most events usually feature a pre-event ceilidh (a type of social event with traditional music, dancing, song, and other forms of entertainment).\n</p><p>Various food vendors will also offer assorted types of traditional Scottish refreshment and sustenance.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_events_in_Scotland">Major events in Scotland</span><span border="1">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Location\n</th>\n<th>Name\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Est%C3%A2ncia_Velha" title="Est\xc3\xa2ncia Velha">Est\xc3\xa2ncia Velha</a>, <a title="Scottish Highland Games Brazil (page does not exist)">Scottish Highland Games Brazil</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Highland_games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 1 August 1997 Canada Post issued \'Highland Games\' designed by Fraser Ross, based on photographs by Andrew Balfour. The 45\xc2\xa2 stamps are perforated 12.5 x 13 and were printed by Canadian Bank Note Company, Limited.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" border="1">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Location<sup id="cite_ref-ccsna_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ccsna-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</th>\n<th>Name\n</th>\n<th>Month Held\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th colspan="3"><a href="/wiki/Alberta" Alberta</a>\n</td>\n<td>Canmore Highland Games<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>August\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Edmonton" Highland Games Championships</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Basque_rural_sports" title="Basque rural sports">Basque rural sports</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Highland_games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ol><li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Cowal"><b><a href="#ref_Cowal">^</a></b></span>  Cowal Highland Gathering can be verified as the world\'s largest highland games on the Official Scottish Tourist Board Website at <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.visitscotland.com/library/highlandgamescalendar">VisitScotland.com</a></li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Canmore"><b><a href="#ref_Canmore">^</a></b></span>  For a modern-day fictional account of this event, see <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.abdn.ac.uk/elphinstone/kist/search/display.php?lwe110.dat"><i>The origins of the Braemar Games Hill Race</i>, by Les Wheeler</a></li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_origins"><b><a href="#ref_origins">^</a></b></span>  Many Highland games web sites contain a brief sketch on the history of the Highland games. Most will mention this hill climb, some referring to it as a story or legend, others as if it were an established fact. Webster, in <i>Scottish Highland Games</i> recounts the story, labelling it as story, or legend only. Thomas Owen Clancy and Barbara E. Crawford, in the Bibliographical essay to chapter 2 (The Formation of the Scottish Kingdom) of <i>The New Penguin History of Scotland</i> state: "Little of significance has been written about the eleventh century kingdom otherwise, except on the dispute over the reliability of the early documentary sources...".</li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Grant"><b><a href="#ref_Grant">^</a></b></span>  As quoted on the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.aboynegames.com/information/history/">history page</a> of the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.aboynegames.com/">Aboyne Highland Gathering</a> web site</li>\n<li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Olympics"><b><a href="#ref_Olympics">^</a></b></span>  The web site of the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20051224150341/http://www.fila-wrestling.com/celtique/index_fichiers/Page322.htm">International Wrestling Association</a> reports rather more expansively on the role of the 1889 Paris event and its effect on the development of the Olympics, considering it to have had a "huge impact" on world sport. An article published in 2004 in the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.csmonitor.com/2004/0519/p01s04-woeu.html">Christian Science Monitor</a> points to two other events, including that of Much Wenlock, a small English village in Shropshire</li></ol>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Highland_games&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 35em; -webkit-column-width: 35em; column-width: 35em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-CHG1-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-CHG1_1-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20120809091943/http://www.cowalgathering.com/spectators.php">"Cowal Highland Gatcitationhering"</a>.
